  "generated_scene": "Mid-morning slack made the cove look paused\u2014no pull on the pilings, just a skin of green glass stippled with rain that had fallen and then given up. The dock\u2019s planks were slick and dark. Kelp hung from the ladder like old ribbons. The funicular track on the bluff stood empty, a thin iron line ending in air.\n\nThe skiff came in low and clean, a municipal gray with the county crest half-scuffed off the bow. The outboard coughed once to let the dock know and then idled in with that modest authority engines have when they\u2019re sure they\u2019ll be obeyed. The Breakwater deputy stood at the bow post, gloved hand on the painter, brim of his cap wet along the edge. He had a face like a good knife\u2014simple, useful, unornamented. Behind him, a second deputy stayed at the tiller and watched the pilings with a mechanic\u2019s patience.\n\nLena had them staged already the way she knew he would want it: crates chalked and numbered; the crowbar that crushed her camera sealed in a polypropylene sleeve; the stack of ledgers wrapped in kitchen twine and sand grit; the transfer printouts in a binder protected under a plastic cutting board because the air never really dried anything here. She stood with her clipboard and the flare scar still visible on the boathouse planks. Jonah was on a crate with his hands visible, jacket off, sea salt dried into the quilted seams. Caleb sat with his back to a piling, wrists zip-tied in front, rain puckering his shirt where he\u2019d sweated through and then cooled. Ivy was near the ladder with a garment bag like a flag folded wrong, heels in her hand, stockings rolled down to protect them from splinters, mouth in a legal line that said control, control, control.\n\nThe deputy stepped across when the skiff\u2019s bow kissed the rubber. He made no show of jumping\u2014he stepped, as if the dock were a hallway floor and the ocean just wall-to-wall rug. He took in the scene the way he always did, left to right, two beats for each person, one for the pile of things that might later be exhibits. The brim of his cap shed a silver curve of water.\n\n\u201cMorning,\u201d he said. \u201cI\u2019m Deputy Salazar, Breakwater detail. Which one of you is Lena Markham?\u201d\n\nLena raised her clipboard slightly. \u201cHere.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re the complainant, and you have chain-of-custody on those?\u201d He indicated the crates with a tilt of the chin.\n\n\u201cYes,\u201d she said. \u201cInitialed. Photographed. Time-stamped. Recorded on the body cam you lent me, which is here.\u201d She touched the camera, its lens fogged from the warm room inside and the cold air here. \u201cSpare SD cards sealed. One\u2019s a clone.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou have a list?\u201d\n\n\u201cTwo copies, one for you, one for evidence.\u201d\n\nHe nodded. He didn\u2019t write anything yet. He let his gaze find the people again. \u201cAnd these are the parties involved?\u201d\n\n\u201cCaleb Dunn,\u201d Lena said, indicating the man by the piling. \u201cJonah Pike.\u201d A hand to the man on the crate. \u201cAnd Ivy Keene.\u201d\n\nIvy fixed a smile on him crisp enough to cut. \u201cCounsel for Eleanor Hart,\u201d she said. \u201cWhich is to say, you and I need to slow down.\u201d\n\n\u201cWe\u2019re already at slack, Ms. Keene,\u201d Salazar said. He didn\u2019t ask how she spelled it. He already knew how to spell things. \u201cYou can slow down in a minute. First I\u2019m going to separate everybody, make sure nobody needs medical, and read some forms.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m fine,\u201d Jonah said quietly. \u201cNo medical.\u201d\n\nCaleb\u2019s lip had a line where he\u2019d bitten it. \u201cThese are unlawful restraints,\u201d he said, lifting his tied hands a fraction. \u201cYou\u2019re looking right at it.\u201d\n\nSalazar looked. \u201cYou resisting right now?\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m stating what you should already know.\u201d\n\n\u201cOkay. Thank you for stating.\u201d He took a folded microfiber towel from his pocket, wiped the rail, and set his notebook there like a clean plate. He glanced toward the boathouse where the flare had scorched the planking in a warped crescent. \u201cWho applied the restraints?\u201d\n\n\u201cI did,\u201d Lena said. \u201cAfter he attempted to move the crate labeled N-5 into the skiff without a bill of lading and after he kicked my evidence bag into the water.\u201d A clear bag sat dripping on the dock with sand and two dead flies clinging to the inside; Lena lifted it with two fingers. \u201cI retrieved it. He knows I retrieved it because he watched.\u201d\n\n\u201cDon\u2019t talk for me,\u201d Caleb said.\n\n\u201cNoted,\u201d Salazar said. He nudged the evidence bag with the butt of his pen. \u201cYou still want to keep using your mouth, Mr. Dunn, you can do that after I read you. The way this works is we do things in the order that keeps it from unraveling when it counts.\u201d He glanced at Jonah. \u201cMr. Pike, you staying put.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019ll go where you put me,\u201d Jonah said. He lifted his hands, palms empty. \u201cI\u2019m not trying to go anywhere.\u201d\n\nIvy stepped in, the garment bag falling against her shin like a fish against a boat. \u201cDeputy, a hearing this morning upheld my client\u2019s competency, which in turn affects authority over these items. There is no emergency removal, no statutory basis to seize\u2014\u201d\n\n\u201cThere\u2019s a basis to not put a forklift on a funicular rated for freight under two hundred pounds,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cThere\u2019s a basis to not spoof an emergency line during a known blackout and there\u2019s a basis to not retaliate against a person making a report.\u201d He pointed with his pen, not at her, but at the chalked numbers. \u201cYou can assert ownership in a minute. Right now I\u2019m going to control the scene.\u201d\n\nHe looked at Lena again. \u201cWhat\u2019s the status of the judge\u2019s order.\u201d\n\n\u201cConfirmed by email. I printed and attached. Page two.\u201d\n\nHe flipped the binder with one finger, used the clean hand. He skimmed. He did not nod; he didn\u2019t like to give away agreement the way other people gave away gum. \u201cOkay,\u201d he said. He looked at the skiff. \u201cBerto, go ahead and set us a drift line on the stern. We\u2019re going to be a while.\u201d\n\nThe second deputy eased the line out and snagged the cleat. The skiff settled into its own small patience.\n\nSalazar turned to Caleb. \u201cMr. Dunn. I\u2019m going to read you your rights while those are still on you. Then I\u2019m going to replace those with mine. You understand?\u201d\n\nCaleb\u2019s jaw worked under a wet lock of hair. \u201cNo probable cause.\u201d\n\n\u201cWe\u2019ll find out. Stand slow.\u201d\n\nCaleb stood. The zip tie chirped where it rubbed his jacket. Salazar read\u2014clear, mid-Atlantic, the words built into him by repetition. Caleb didn\u2019t answer yes or no to the questions meant to elicit those words. Salazar didn\u2019t push. When he was done, he clipped away the tie in one clean snip and took Caleb\u2019s wrists, turning them with a nurse\u2019s habit around fragile things. He cuffed him low and to the front. He checked circulation by pressing a finger and watching the skin pink back up. He double-locked the ratchets.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re under arrest for attempted removal of property under disputed guardianship, interference with a communications system, and tampering with evidence,\u201d he said. \u201cYou\u2019ll get a paper. It\u2019ll read cleaner.\u201d\n\n\u201cCharge the tide while you\u2019re at it,\u201d Caleb said.\n\n\u201cCharges aren\u2019t weather,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cThey\u2019re words. Words have rules.\u201d He turned to the second deputy. \u201cBerto, you want Mr. Dunn at bow. Keep him dry if you can.\u201d\n\nBerto guided Caleb toward the skiff without having to touch him much. He didn\u2019t take the man\u2019s elbow in a way that would make it a fight; he stepped in a way that made the boat the only place to go.\n\nIvy\u2019s smile had vanished. \u201cYou will not take custody of those crates,\u201d she said, pointing at N-3 as if the chalk mark could move. \u201cThey contain heirloom nursery pieces that\u2014\u201d\n\n\u201cThat currently figure into an investigation,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cI\u2019m seizing them lawfully with a receipt issued to the custodian of the premises, copied to counsel of record. You\u2019re on the CC line already; I read it.\u201d He glanced over his shoulder to the hill. \u201cThe custodian is?\u201d\n\n\u201cMara Hart,\u201d Lena said. \u201cShe\u2019s at the top of the stairs with the keys.\u201d\n\n\u201cGreat. Go get me her signature.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m not participating in a seizure,\u201d Ivy said.\n\n\u201cYou don\u2019t have to,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cYou can stand there and say no at me all day. It will make no difference to the paper, which is the part that matters.\u201d\n\nJonah slid off the crate as if to help, then thought better of it, hands still visible. \u201cYou want me where.\u201d\n\n\u201cWhere you are is fine,\u201d Salazar said, moving past him to kneel by the nearest crate. He ran his glove along the edge where the lid met the side, feeling for telltales. He found a hair\u2014a human hair\u2014stuck in caught varnish and paused just long enough to let his brain take a picture. Then he took an actual picture with his phone, angling the lens to avoid glare.\n\n\u201cWhat\u2019s in N-1,\u201d he said.\n\n\u201cCradle pieces from the nursery,\u201d Lena said. \u201cPaint samples matched to the original receipts.\u201d\n\n\u201cWho packed it.\u201d\n\n\u201cJonah under Caleb\u2019s instruction.\u201d\n\n\u201cMr. Pike?\u201d Salazar asked without looking up.\n\nJonah looked at the water once and back. \u201cYes,\u201d he said. \u201cThat\u2019s right.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou have a bill of lading.\u201d\n\n\u201cCaleb has a list,\u201d Jonah said. \u201cNot a bill.\u201d\n\n\u201cDid you sign a 1099 for removal.\u201d\n\n\u201cI don\u2019t know what that is,\u201d Jonah said. It was not bravado. It was a fact that lived in his hands and not in his head.\n\nSalazar stood up. He took a roll of red evidence tape from his coat, snapped a strip free, and sealed the crate across the seam. He wrote with a fine Sharpie, neat as an architect. Date. Time. Initials. Location. N-1. He did N-2 and N-3 the same way, in a rhythm that soothed something in the morning. Rain stitched across his cap brim and off the dock in little hard-luck coins.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re not going to cut into them here,\u201d Ivy said, watching his pen like it might be a blade. \u201cThey\u2019re antiques.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m not going to cut them anywhere,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cI\u2019m going to hold them. Later, in a dry room with a camera running, a table, gloves you can approve of, and everyone invited, somebody else will open them with a screwdriver.\u201d He held up the roll, the end of the tape sticking to his glove. \u201cThis is just to keep the future honest.\u201d\n\nHe pointed to the crowbar in the bag. \u201cThat\u2019s the tool used on a camera in the generator shed.\u201d\n\n\u201cYes,\u201d Lena said.\n\n\u201cYou watch that happen,\u201d Salazar asked.\n\n\u201cI watched the result,\u201d Lena said. \u201cMy camera went black after a person walked in with that. The shed cam recorded the angle and a sleeve seam. Then it died. The sleeve seam matches the jacket in the boathouse now.\u201d She pointed to a dark nylon jacket hung over a cleat to drain, its sleeve patched with gray tape. \u201cJonah will tell you who wore it.\u201d\n\n\u201cJonah?\u201d Salazar asked, turning his face not unkindly.\n\nJonah swallowed. \u201cCaleb.\u201d\n\n\u201cOkay,\u201d Salazar said. He made a note as if writing Caleb in that notebook changed nothing and everything. He turned to Jonah, let the quiet between them settle. \u201cMr. Pike, you\u2019re going to come with me also. You\u2019re not under arrest. You\u2019re being detained for questioning. I\u2019m going to pat you down for weapons. You have anything on you I should know will stab me.\u201d\n\n\u201cNo,\u201d Jonah said. He raised his arms away from his sides. \u201cNo knives.\u201d\n\nSalazar patted him down, clean. He found a brass fishing weight, a pocket screw, a paper twist of licorice. He set the licorice back in the pocket like a dad would and moved on. He put a light hand on Jonah\u2019s upper arm and left it there only long enough for Jonah to understand it was a guide and not a hook.\n\nIvy said, \u201cDeputy, while you perform your ritual, understand that any statements my client\u2014\u201d\n\n\u201cMs. Keene,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cIf you\u2019re counsel for Eleanor Hart, you\u2019re not counsel for Mr. Dunn unless he says, and even then I\u2019m not holding my breath. You want to represent Mr. Pike too, I\u2019m going to need to see a letter you wrote yourself, and I\u2019m going to watch you not write it on that dock.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re discourteous.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m busy,\u201d he said, without heat. He looked at Lena. \u201cWhere\u2019s your phone.\u201d\n\n\u201cIn my pocket.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou recorded the judge\u2019s assistant\u2019s acknowledgment?\u201d\n\n\u201cEmail and call log,\u201d she said. \u201cScreenshots printed. Thumb drive.\u201d\n\n\u201cGood.\u201d He took her copies, slid them into an envelope that said E-1. He printed her name on it. He looked up the stairs. Mara had appeared at the break in the guardrail, key ring on a carabiner the size of a fist. She was breathing like she\u2019d come down the slope at a run.\n\n\u201cMs. Hart,\u201d he said. \u201cWe\u2019re going to do a property receipt. You\u2019ll sign as custodian. These crates will go to the evidence locker in town. I\u2019ll send you the number. You\u2019ll call me if anyone calls you. You\u2019ll take no further action until I tell you where to sit.\u201d\n\nMara nodded without arguing. \u201cI\u2019ll sign,\u201d she said. She had grease on one thumb that never seemed to fully lift; it left a ghost on the paper next to her name.\n\nCaleb watched the pen shape her signature and made a sound that wasn\u2019t a word. He tested the cuffs and stopped when they reminded him what they were.\n\n\u201cYou want to keep glaring, Mr. Dunn,\u201d Salazar said mildly, \u201ckeep it up. It won\u2019t go on paper.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019ll put it on mine,\u201d Caleb said. \u201cI\u2019ll file for suppression on half of this and sanctions on the other half.\u201d\n\n\u201cI hope your coffee\u2019s good,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cIt might take a while.\u201d\n\nHe gestured for Berto, and together they slid the first crate toward the skiff, balancing weight, keeping fingers out of the pinch points. They worked like men who had moved too many heavy things badly once and decided to move them well forever afterward. The boat dipped and then held. The deck took the second crate as neatly. Salazar sealed the bedline with more tape he\u2019d initialed and crossed the strip so the crate and the skiff married under the law.\n\nHe turned to Ivy again. \u201cDo you intend to accompany Mr. Dunn.\u201d\n\n\u201cI intend to make sure you don\u2019t hide him,\u201d she said.\n\n\u201cWe don\u2019t hide things,\u201d Salazar said. \u201cWe log them. And we sit under fluorescent lights that hum like cheap bees. You can follow us in your heels.\u201d He looked at her bare feet. \u201cOr not.\u201d\n\nShe slid the heels into the garment bag, zipped its mouth like a wound sutured by a distracted intern. \u201cI\u2019ll be right behind you.\u201d\n\n\u201cFine,\u201d he said. \u201cNo lights, no siren. It\u2019s not that kind of day.\u201d\n\nHe took one last slow survey. The burnt scallop on the boards. The ladder slick with kelp. The way Lena\u2019s knuckles had faded from white back to their normal color in the last five minutes. He wrote something else down. He used block capitals this time.\n\n\u201cYou have any more footage of the subpanel,\u201d he asked Lena, as if this were just another item you check off before lunch.\n\n\u201cCass has the transfer files. I mirrored them to you last night. If your inbox does what mine did, check spam.\u201d\n\n\u201cI already checked,\u201d he said, and something about that \u201calready\u201d made the dock feel held.\n\nHe looked at Jonah. \u201cYou ready.\u201d\n\nJonah nodded once. \u201cYes.\u201d\n\nHe looked at Caleb. \u201cYou ready.\u201d\n\nCaleb didn\u2019t answer.\n\n\u201cThat\u2019s fine,\u201d Salazar said. He tilted his head at Berto. \u201cBow.\u201d\n\nThey moved. The skiff took them. The crates settled against the ribs with a domestic sound, as if they were just boxes that had always belonged to boats. Salazar stepped back onto the dock to take the last signatures, to hand Mara the yellow copy and Lena the pink, to give Ivy nothing because she had refused paper.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019ll email me,\u201d Ivy said tightly.\n\n\u201cI already did,\u201d he said. \u201cCheck spam.\u201d\n\nA gull landed, set two deliberate feet on the tape edge like it understood boundaries. The tide didn\u2019t pull. The pilings didn\u2019t complain. Procedure filled the air the way weather had earlier, and it was better. Salazar nodded to Lena once. It wasn\u2019t a handshake, but it was the dock\u2019s version of one.\n\n\u201cScene is secure,\u201d he said, into his shoulder mic. \u201cThree detainees: one under arrest, one detained, one counsel. Evidence in transit. Copy.\u201d\n\n\u201cCopy,\u201d came back, small and tinny and sufficient.\n\nHe stepped into the skiff. Berto cast off. The line went slack and came taut and then slack again, the simplest conversation in the world. The motor cleared its throat like an old teacher and then spoke. The skiff turned her face toward town. On the dock, Lena watched until the gray of the county seal and the red stripes of tape made a single moving shape and then smaller than that. She looked down. The burn ring held its place on the board, a dark smile that meant exactly what it looked like: heat, and then a line, and then someone in charge of the next thing. She put her palm flat against the wood, felt nothing move beneath it, and began to pick up the wet twine.",

(+)\"\"\"\n\nHere is the ending of the previous scene:\n\"\"\"He took one last slow survey. The burnt scallop on the boards. The ladder slick with kelp. The way Lena\u2019s knuckles had faded from white back to their normal color in the last five minutes. He wrote something else down. He used block capitals this time.\n\u201cYou have any more footage of the subpanel,\u201d he asked Lena, as if this were just another item you check off before lunch.\n\u201cCass has the transfer files. The line went slack and came taut and then slack again, the simplest conversation in the world. The motor cleared its throat like an old teacher and then spoke. The skiff turned her face toward town. On the dock, Lena watched until the gray of the county seal and the red stripes of tape made a single moving shape and then smaller than that. She looked down. The burn ring held its place on the board, a dark smile that meant exactly what it looked like: heat, and then a line, and then someone in charge of the next thing. She put her palm flat against the wood, felt nothing move beneath it, and began to pick up the wet twine.\"\"\""

Someone had set out two paper cups of coffee and then forgotten them; a skin had formed on one, moonsilver and edged brown. Lena, you\u2019re fine where you are.\u201d\n\nLena had a coil of wet twine in her coat pocket and the smell of tide salt still on her sleeves. Her hair was damp along the neck. She pulled her chair in, adjusted, watched the laptop screen show the empty thumbnail squares reorganize into a single window with a seal and a name.\n\n\u201cDepartment Twenty,\u201d said the bailiff\u2019s flat voice from somewhere off-screen. \u201cOn calendar: In re Matlock, ex parte petition for temporary guardianship\u2014competency disputed. He sat at the far end of the table like a man putting distance between himself and a campfire he had started. \u201cPetitioner\u2019s counsel.\u201d He glanced at the second chair at his side, empty.
